      '\r\n' +
      'Correct possible race conditions during device removal.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Previously, a scheduled work item to reset a LUN could still execute\r\n' +
      'after the device was removed, leading to use-after-free and other\r\n' +
      'resource access issues.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This race condition occurs because the abort handler may schedule a LUN\r\n' +
      'reset concurrently with device removal via sdev_destroy(), leading to\r\n' +
      'use-after-free and improper access to freed resources.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '  - Check in the device reset handler if the device is still present in\r\n' +
      "    the controller's SCSI device list before running if not, the reset\r\n" +
      '    is skipped.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '  - Cancel any pending TMF work that has not started in sdev_destroy().\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '  - Ensure device freeing in sdev_destroy() is done while holding the\r\n' +
      '    LUN reset mutex to avoid races with ongoing resets. | Severity UNKNOWN',

    title: 'CVE-2025-68375 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'perf/x86 Fix NULL event access...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2025-68375',
    pubDate: 'Wed, 24 Dec 2025 11:16:00 GMT',
    content: '[[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'perf/x86 Fix NULL event access and potential PEBS record loss\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'When intel_pmu_drain_pebs_icl() is called to drain PEBS records, the\r\n' +
      'perf_event_overflow() could be called to process the last PEBS record.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'While perf_event_overflow() could trigger the interrupt throttle and\r\n' +
      'stop all events of the group, like what the below call-chain shows.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'perf_event_overflow()\r\n' +
      '  -> __perf_event_overflow()\r\n' +
      '    ->__perf_event_account_interrupt()\r\n' +
      '      -> perf_event_throttle_group()\r\n' +
      '        -> perf_event_throttle()\r\n' +
      '          -> event->pmu->stop()\r\n' +
      '            -> x86_pmu_stop()\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The side effect of stopping the events is that all corresponding event\r\n' +
      'pointers in cpuc->events[] array are cleared to NULL.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Assume there are two PEBS events (event a and event b) in a group. When\r\n' +
      'intel_pmu_drain_pebs_icl() calls perf_event_overflow() to process the\r\n' +
      'last PEBS record of PEBS event a, interrupt throttle is triggered and\r\n' +
      'all pointers of event a and event b are cleared to NULL. Then\r\n' +
      'intel_pmu_drain_pebs_icl() tries to process the last PEBS record of\r\n' +
      'event b and encounters NULL pointer access.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'To avoid this issue, move cpuc->events[] clearing from x86_pmu_stop()\r\n' +
      "to x86_pmu_del(). It's safe since cpuc->active_mask or\r\n" +
      'cpuc->pebs_enabled is always checked before access the event pointer\r\n' +
      'from cpuc->events[]. | Severity UNKNOWN',

      'could be validate_xmit_unreadable_skb(), but then otoh it would be\r\n' +

  {
    title: 'CVE-2022-50700 In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'wifi ath10k Delay the unmappi...',
    link: 'https//nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2022-50700',
    pubDate: 'Wed, 24 Dec 2025 11:15:00 GMT',
    content: '[[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'wifi ath10k Delay the unmapping of the buffer\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'On WCN3990, we are seeing a rare scenario where copy engine hardware is\r\n' +
      'sending a copy complete interrupt to the host driver while still\r\n' +
      'processing the buffer that the driver has sent, this is leading into an\r\n' +
      'SMMU fault triggering kernel panic. This is happening on copy engine\r\n' +
      'channel 3 (CE3) where the driver normally enqueues WMI commands to the\r\n' +
      'firmware. Upon receiving a copy complete interrupt, host driver will\r\n' +
      'immediately unmap and frees the buffer presuming that hardware has\r\n' +
      'processed the buffer. In the issue case, upon receiving copy complete\r\n' +
      'interrupt, host driver will unmap and free the buffer but since hardware\r\n' +
      'is still accessing the buffer (which in this case got unmapped in\r\n' +
      'parallel), SMMU hardware will trigger an SMMU fault resulting in a\r\n' +
      'kernel panic.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'In order to avoid this, as a work around, add a delay before unmapping\r\n' +
      'the copy engine source DMA buffer. This is conditionally done for\r\n' +
      'WCN3990 and only for the CE3 channel where issue is seen.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Below is the crash signature\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'wifi smmu error kernel [ 10.120965] arm-smmu 15000000.iommu Unhandled\r\n' +
      'context fault fsr=0x402, iova=0x7fdfd8ac0,\r\n' +
      'fsynr=0x500003,cbfrsynra=0xc1, cb=6 arm-smmu 15000000.iommu Unhandled\r\n' +
      'context faultfsr=0x402, iova=0x7fe06fdc0, fsynr=0x710003,\r\n' +
      'cbfrsynra=0xc1, cb=6 qcom-q6v5-mss 4080000.remoteproc fatal error\r\n' +
      'received err_qdi.c1040EFwlan_process0x1WLAN RT0x2091\r\n' +
      'cmnos_thread.c3998Asserted in copy_engine.cAXI_ERROR_DETECTED2149\r\n' +
      'remoteproc remoteproc0 crash detected in\r\n' +
      '4080000.remoteproc type fatal error 3> remoteproc remoteproc0\r\n' +
      'handling crash #1 in 4080000.remoteproc\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'pc  __arm_lpae_unmap+0x500/0x514\r\n' +
      'lr  __arm_lpae_unmap+0x4bc/0x514\r\n' +

    contentSnippet: '[[In the Linux kernel, the following vulnerability has been resolved\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'wifi ath10k Delay the unmapping of the buffer\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'On WCN3990, we are seeing a rare scenario where copy engine hardware is\r\n' +
      'sending a copy complete interrupt to the host driver while still\r\n' +
      'processing the buffer that the driver has sent, this is leading into an\r\n' +
      'SMMU fault triggering kernel panic. This is happening on copy engine\r\n' +
      'channel 3 (CE3) where the driver normally enqueues WMI commands to the\r\n' +
      'firmware. Upon receiving a copy complete interrupt, host driver will\r\n' +
      'immediately unmap and frees the buffer presuming that hardware has\r\n' +
      'processed the buffer. In the issue case, upon receiving copy complete\r\n' +
      'interrupt, host driver will unmap and free the buffer but since hardware\r\n' +
      'is still accessing the buffer (which in this case got unmapped in\r\n' +
      'parallel), SMMU hardware will trigger an SMMU fault resulting in a\r\n' +
      'kernel panic.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'In order to avoid this, as a work around, add a delay before unmapping\r\n' +
      'the copy engine source DMA buffer. This is conditionally done for\r\n' +
      'WCN3990 and only for the CE3 channel where issue is seen.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +

      "their 'virt' parameter, but the check itself doesn't make much sense.\r\n" +
      'The condition used today appears to be a historical accident.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'The sanity-check condition\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '\tif ((virt >= PAGE_END)  (virt  VMALLOC_START)) {\r\n' +
      '\t\t[ ... warning here ... ]\r\n' +
      '\t\treturn\r\n' +
      '\t}\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '... can only be true for the KASAN shadow region or the module region,\r\n' +
      "and there's no reason to exclude these specifically for creating and\r\n" +
      'updateing mappings.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'When arm64 support was first upstreamed in commit\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '  c1cc1552616d0f35 ("arm64 MMU initialisation")\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '... the condition was\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '\tif (virt  VMALLOC_START) {\r\n' +
      '\t\t[ ... warning here ... ]\r\n' +
      '\t\treturn\r\n' +
      '\t}\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'At the time, VMALLOC_START was the lowest kernel address, and this was\r\n' +
      "checking whether 'virt' would be translated via TTBR1.\r\n" +
      '\r\n' +
      'Subsequently in commit\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '  14c127c957c1c607 ("arm64 mm Flip kernel VA space")\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '... the condition was changed to\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '\tif ((virt >= VA_START)  (virt  VMALLOC_START)) {\r\n' +
      '\t\t[ ... warning here ... ]\r\n' +
      '\t\treturn\r\n' +
      '\t}\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'This appear to have been a thinko. The commit moved the linear map to\r\n' +
      'the bottom of the kernel address space, with VMALLOC_START being at the\r\n' +
      'halfway point. The old condition would warn for changes to the linear\r\n' +
      'map below this, and at the time VA_START was the end of the linear map.\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Subsequently we cleaned up the naming of VA_START in commit\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '  77ad4ce69321abbe ("arm64 memory rename VA_START to PAGE_END")\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '... keeping the erroneous condition as\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      '\tif ((virt >= PAGE_END)  (virt  VMALLOC_START)) {\r\n' +
      '\t\t[ ... warning here ... ]\r\n' +
      '\t\treturn\r\n' +
      '\t}\r\n' +
      '\r\n' +
      'Correct the condition to check against the start of the TTBR1 address\r\n' +
      'space, which is currently PAGE_OFFSET. This simplifies the logic, and\r\n' +
      'more clearly matches the "outside kernel range" message in the warning. | Severity UNKNOWN',
